  <span id="freeText15662293514024594042" style="display:none">The tv show is one of my absolute favourites, so going into this book, I didn't actually have very high expectations. I'd heard that the book was very different to the show, and since I love the show, I wasn't too sure on what to expect. However, this book was exactly what I needed to feed my cravings whilst the tv show is on break until later in the year!<br /><br />The story is different, and I liked hearing about the characters that have no appearance on the show. I mean, anything that involves Bellamy Blake and Clarke Griffin I am bound to love. For me, the story was a compelling read which I finished in one day. Although, if I hadn't watched the show before I'd read the book, I highly doubt I would've liked it as much as I did. It got 3 stars due to me recognising that I wouldn't have enjoyed it as much without watching the tv show, although, I would definitely recommend this to any 'The 100' fans waiting for the show to come back!<br /><br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615631316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11883024624286115095">I quite enjoyed this book. <br/><br/>Loved seeing the different perspectives and flashbacks, those added a little something extra to the novel.<br/><br/>It was also fun picking out the similarities and differences to the TV Show, which I love so much.<br/><br/>I didn't feel a great connection to the characters in this book, but there was definitely something there, so hopefully it grows when I read the next 2 books!<br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1089001441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089001441" />
    <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet"><img alt="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387046887p2/13567836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089001441?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet">Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17370280-the-hundred">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=love-triangle-menage-orgy">love-triangle-menage-orgy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian">dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089001441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11956543228361419964"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The door slid open, and Clarke knew it was time to die. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Too many POV's for my taste... (Clarke and Bellamy's POV was perfectly fine for me, but Wells and Glass was okay in the start, but then I started losing interest in them, specially Wells..) , but I love ALL the Bellarke scenes! And yes, you have guessed it, I'm a HUGE Bellarke fan! Though, I had expected a love-hate relationship between Clarke and Bellamy like in the TV-show, but I guess you kinda have to separate the book and t</span>
  <span id="freeText11956543228361419964" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The door slid open, and Clarke knew it was time to die. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Too many POV's for my taste... (Clarke and Bellamy's POV was perfectly fine for me, but Wells and Glass was okay in the start, but then I started losing interest in them, specially Wells..) , but I love ALL the Bellarke scenes! And yes, you have guessed it, I'm a HUGE Bellarke fan! Though, I had expected a love-hate relationship between Clarke and Bellamy like in the TV-show, but I guess you kinda have to separate the book and the show, because the were A LOT of different from each other.. and I mean HELL of a lot too. But at least we got at many Bellarke scenes, which was the only reason I decided to read this book :P <br><blockquote>
  <b>*AND NO, I WOULDN'T LIKED THIS BOOK HAD I NOT SEEN THE TV SHOW FIRST AND LOVED THE SHOW!*</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419567352i/13093218.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I came for you,” he said softly.<br>Her face assumed an expression that broke through the barriers, a mixture of sorrow, frustration, and pity that seemed to travel from Clarke’s eyes straight into his chest.<br>“I wish you hadn’t.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Now, on to the stupid love triangle... I must say, I HATE love triangles... so I freaking hope that in the next book, there will be NONE! Wells is so in love that he is crazy (that's what I think at least.. Some might think it's cute, but I think it's a little too much.) He could be a cool friend if he cooled down a bit, and.. I don't know? I don't mind him being in love with Clarke, but what he did? Man, that was insane! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419570312ra/13093675.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>His stomach twisted strangely as he thought back to the scene by the fire, the flames flickering over Clarke’s determined face. He’d never known a girl who was so beautiful and intense at once.<br>Bellamy leaned back with a sigh and closed his eyes, wondering how long it would take until she stopped being the last person he thought about before he fell asleep.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Bellamy... I love him. Specially, Bob Morley as Bellamy.. Damn, he's just the perfect one.. In the TV show, he's dangerous, sexy, badass and a bad boy.. But in the book though, he all that, but he also not? I don't know how to explain.. He's just too kind to be a bad boy yet, I think.. ? Perhaps it will come.. I sure hope so! I do love a bad boy!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419570312ra/13093676.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I just—I couldn’t let you go. You would’ve been killed.”<br>“So you let Thalia die instead. Because you get to decide who lives and who dies.” He started to protest, but she kept going, shaking with rage. “Tonight was a mistake. You destroy everything you touch.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Clarke was adorable :)! She's just a girl trying to save her best friend. I love her. I felt no hatred, no dislike toward her at all, though I was afraid I would because of the love triangle I know was going to be in the book. But she handled it well, I must say :) Clarke is a really strong girl, who's been trough a hell of a lot. Loosing both of her parents, being betrayed by her best friend/boyfriend and sent to earth... She's a independent 17 years old girl who knows how to take care of herself, yet help other at the same time. I just love her. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419570312ra/13093677.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The hundred might have been the first humans to set foot on the planet in three centuries, but they weren’t alone.<br>Some people had never left. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book was better than I thought it was going to be, and I can't wait to see how the journey will continue. <br>Though there was quite many writing mistakes, making it hard to read at times, it was an enjoyable reading, and I cannot wait to continue reading the series :) Since the TV show really aren't following the book series (as it seems after reading this one), then I seriously have NO idea what will happen... So I'm genially curious on what will happen! :D On to the next one!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419570312ra/13093678.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>Rate: 4/3 stars.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11956543228361419964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1028828260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1028828260" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17389678-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145890p2/17389678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1028828260?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/17389678-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">chocolate strawberries fans aka overpowering chocolate taste. Same case. Romance &gt; dystopia.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17389678-jess?shelf=today-i-feel-masochistic">today-i-feel-masochistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17389678-jess?shelf=the-dystopian-lot">the-dystopian-lot</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028828260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13989421693299844528"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> To save the girl he loved, he’d have to endanger the entire human race. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>Pick up your shit and get with the fucking program, Wells. You’re on what <i>appears</i> (objective word here) to be a <b>post-apocolyptic</b> toxic (but not fucking explained) dystopian Earth. How about you save the selfishness for a rainy day and take out some of that <b>much needed</b> self preservation. <br/><br/>If <i>The 100</i> was anything, it surely, not even in it’s dreams, wouldn't be a post-apocolypitic dystopia. <b>It’s a fucking romance </b></span>
  <span id="freeText13989421693299844528" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> To save the girl he loved, he’d have to endanger the entire human race. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br /><br />Pick up your shit and get with the fucking program, Wells. You’re on what <i>appears</i> (objective word here) to be a <b>post-apocolyptic</b> toxic (but not fucking explained) dystopian Earth. How about you save the selfishness for a rainy day and take out some of that <b>much needed</b> self preservation. <br /><br />If <i>The 100</i> was anything, it surely, not even in it’s dreams, wouldn't be a post-apocolypitic dystopia. <b>It’s a fucking romance novel</b>. Do not be fooled (I took the bait for you. I’m saving you the time and trouble, right now, if that’s what you’ve wandered here for. It’s not too late to save yourself). <br /><br />Now, in terms of the world building spiel I’m about to embark on, I have no idea as to whether or not I am correct in my assumptions. As perceptive as I am, the lack of <b>information</b> really hinders what a girl can do. In the context of <i>The 100</i>, Earth has undergone<b> “the Catacylsm”</b>. Let’s start off with what the fuck that is. I assume that it was some pivotal event to do with toxic fumes, radiation, and genetic mutation, but that’s just going off general slips of mouths. <b>There isn’t even a semblance of fucks given to world-buillding.</b> It’s exactly like when I was six and my babysitter dumped a shit tonne of disjointed lego pieces at my feet and told me to conjure some award-winning princess castle. How the fuck was I meant to do that?! I had the fucking pieces, sure, but did I look like a fucking architect? I’d never played with lego before, get fucking real. Take this story and apply to <i>The 100</i>. <br /><br />I should have seen the signs of a poor dystopia. They were fed to me, straight from the start. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>…setting fire to the <b>Eden Tree</b>, the sapling that had been carried onto <b>Phoenix</b> right before the <b>Exodus</b>.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />That was thrown straight at my face from the very first pages. I wouldn’t swallowed my complaint had it been explained, but no. I got no explanation, and the stupid special tree was never again heard from. <br /><br />What the fuck is an Eden Tree, the heck is Phoenix, and I get that it’s before some Exodus event, but what the fuck is it? I just got into the book. I don’t have a repository of information about shit I’ve never read before. <br /><br /><i>The 100</i> crafts its storyline on the basis that 100 convicts are banished into the seemingly toxic lands of Earth (from a fucking floating spaceship) in order to be guinea pigs. Fair enough. <b>But</b> the point of their journey is to <i>prove</i> that<b> “Earth was safe…”</b>. <b>SAFE FROM WHAT?!</b> Just explain it, a little, just a little to me. I’ve got no idea what the fuck this society fears except for vague hints that are worse than a teenager's attempt to discreetly hint at the fact that they know some special secret. I drop better hints than that. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>…second nuclear winter…<br /><br />All the livestock had been eliminated in the middle of the first century. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />That’s just great and all but I’ve got no compassion to give to something that I have no idea about. And jeebus, looks like they’ve been on that fucking ship for over a hundred years. That’s quite the history. So why won’t you just fucking tell me some of it?<br /><br />Apart from the lack of world building, the main problem with this fucking book was the <b>TSTL EVERYONES</b>. Everyone is fucking motivated by love. Get dropped on a toxic Earth potentially ridden with a multitude of diseases, radiation, and a fucked up climate—<b>YES! LET’S DO IT FOR LOVE</b>. <br /><br />I felt <b>no relation, compassion, care, empathy</b> and whatever the fuck describes the connection between reader and character. I just wanted to bang their heads together and sit them in a lifelong seminar entitled,<b> “HOW TO GAIN COMMON SENSE AND USE IT”</b>. <br /><br />Love’s a big theme in the book. The amount of<i> I love you’s</i> was astounding—far beyond what you would find in a YA book, in general, (especially in a first-in-a-series) let alone a fucking dystopia. It was bloody <b>drowning</b> in declarations of love, from start to fucking finish. <br /><br />Case in point:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “I love you,” she whispered, needing desperately to say it. I love you I love you I love you….. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Generally we build up to the climatic, tension oozing declaration that is just a little bit shy, apprehensive and mostly <i>out of place</i>, but I’ll give props to this book for fucking conventionality. It goes for the full frontal force of love. And you know why? <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> Because there were FOUR Point of Views.</b>
</blockquote> <br /><br />That’s right. No need to pull out the fingers to count. Its all the fingers on your hand (bar the thumb). That is ridiculous. And can you tell how chuffed I am that everyone single bloody one of the four has a lovely element of romance in their fucking storyline (here’s a clue: I had to pick up my eyeballs because they rolled right out of my eye sockets). (PS. Having four prominent characters means that I have to write <b>four</b> separate sections of criticism. How beautiful.) <br /><br />Two characters who have <b>no business</b> being on this, seemingly, suicidal mission, jump on it anyway, because fuck death, it’s all about <b>love</b>. Everyone has a fucking <b>hero syndrome</b>.<br /><br />Wells is the most idiotic and boring character that I have had the misfortune of reading. Something possesses him, luring him into thinking that by adding himself to the list of potential casualties by whatever the fuck Earth has in stall, he’ll be forgiven and earn the love of his ex-girlfriend—who he fucking betrayed. That stupid quote at the top of this review? That’s Wells and his selfish as fuck of an attempt at logic. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> The girl he though he’d lost was still in there, somewhere, and in that instant, he knew: He could make her love him again. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />If she doesn’t fucking love you Wells then let life develop at it’s own pace. There’s no need to play God. You’d think the idiot has better things to do, <b>like worry about the fact that he’s surrounded on a toxic Earth with 98 other criminals</b>. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> This was where he’d kissed Clarke for the very first time on Earth—and for what was surely the last time in his life. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />Take the hormones down a notch you idiot. Keeping in mind that that stupid thought was the one occupying his mind when <b>people just died in the aftermath of a fucking fire</b>. If only he put half that effort into surviving, he certainly has the motivation to. Society could be fucking thriving. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> Even if she kissed someone else—even if she wanted to be with someone else—he would always be there for her. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />First things first, as fucking if. Second—I don’t give two fucks. It’s obviously been affirmed that Wells cares deeply for Clarke. I only had to read about it interlaced throughout his soppy thoughts, which amounts to 8 solo chapters. <br /><br />Bellamy, in essence, is also empowered to risk his life, jumping on the suicidal expedition to Earth all for love. But, it’s slightly <i>more</i> noble. It’s a big brother looks out for the kiddie sister sitch, if you feel. So I’m not hating. I can understand that kind of bond because I’m not heartless. <br /><br />That being said, Bellamy is not excused from the wrath of hate. He is a fucking douchebag.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>...[he] titled his face toward the sun, exhaling as the warmth seeped into his skin. It was almost as nice as being in bed with a girl. Maybe even better, because the sun would never ask him what he was thinking.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Now I believe in equality, equal rights and whatnot (and that’s both ways, mind you). Am I to assume that Bellamy is a sexist pig who is condemning the female population for having a brain and using it to fucking think? I know the facade for that nonchalant phrase was most probably to establish Bellamy as a philandering dick but honestly, it missed the mark. All I see is a face that I desperately want to punch (that’s right, lest I be too feminine with a girly slap). <br /><br />And who is to deny Bellamy a chance at love. Certainly not a dystopia! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> He’d never known a girl who was so beautiful and intense at once…[he wondered] how long it would take until she stopped being the last person he thought about before he fell asleep. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />So of course, if we’re doing the YA dystopia, time’s a ticking, and thus in comes the <b>insta!love</b>. What a fucking joke. Let’s be honest here Bellamy, it’ll be pretty fucking easy to forget her since, you know, y’all don’t know each other, bar one lustful encounter. Barely even that. <br /><br />Plus, if we’re doing the whole <b>romance as plot</b> thing of course its obligatory for the <b>almighty transcendental moment</b>. If my eyeballs roll away from me and you find them, please bury them someplace nice and mark it with<b> “Jess’ eyeballs out rolled themselves, doomed by the YA transcendental moment. She shall be congratulated for having endured so many, over and over again.”</b> That’d be nice, wouldn’t it. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> The world around them faded away as Earth become nothing more than a swirl of pungent scents and damp air that made him press himself close to her….They were the only two people on Earth. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />HAHAHA! (that was done over obnoxiously—it’s better that way) Of course their chemistry has melted away the transient nature of the human condition. Of bloooody course. <br /><br />Glass, one of the two female POVs, is segregated from the 100, left back on Earth with her former beau or whatever the fuck they are now. She encapsulates the romance plot cliche as well, while we’re at it. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> The only way to save Luke’s heart was to break it.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />That is it. Who came up with that stupid notion that has seemed to ingrain itself into every fucking YA protagonist’s mind. Stop it. The only way this swings is into a cesspool of complications because her fucking plot line was just <i>romance, romance, romance</i>. You’d think that having a character left on the ship would mean that the audience get to see a deeper explanation into the <b>political drift, socioeconomic divide and general details about the post apocalyptic event</b>, but fuck it. This is about <b>
  <i>lurrrveeeee</i>
</b>.<br /> <br />To be honest, in the end Clarke was the only character I could give any care to. Her characterisation isn’t deep. None of them are. I didn’t empathise with her. Because she put herself into her own situation (I said it, I’m sorry but she’s TSTL). Plus she fucking stole the <b>fickle crown</b> right off my head; just stuck her hand out and ripped it from me. There’s a <b>sad</b> attempt at a <b>love triangle</b>, and of course Clarke oscillates like a fucking pendulum because we need to establish that even in desolation, Clarke remains the apple of everyone’s fucking eye. <br /><br />And are you honestly expecting me to believe that her best friend, on her fucking deathbed, is just dying to hand out love advice. It's always <i>"Clarke, Clarke, Clarke, you're gorge and he loves you"</i>. It's <b>never</b> <i>"Clarke, get over yourself. I, your best friend, am fucking dying. Who gives a fuck about who loves who."</i><br /><br />Structurally, I didn’t like it. It read more like something that belonged on the box that projects images to us while we mindlessly gaze into the beyond (and thus I understand the hype of the tv show). It’s written <b>better</b> as a script. It was blandly written so don’t expect anything fancy, like a metaphor that will have you tittering (cause I would’ve reported back if there were any). Now I’m not saying that I want Oscar Wilde to jazz it up, but please, do something creative. Instead of<b> “he said quietly”</b>, why don’t we try<b> “he whispered, voice tickling the air”</b> (I don’t know, don’t judge me on that). <br /><br /><b>That being said</b>, I will <b>praise</b> it’s consistency. It was consistently written in this action manner. It isn’t clunky and the author is <b>not</b> indecisive. She knows her style and she stuck through with it, right up until the end. <br /><br />Keep in mind that this is written just as you would watch it on the television screen. Scenes cut off so that you will have to imagine them. Cliffhangers occur as the POV moves onto another person, and the storyline is never returned to. And each POV is written in present tense with a <b>jarring</b> flashback smack bang in the middle, à la Arrow. It tells a <b>large chunk of the storyline through flashbacks</b> (but of course that has nothing to do with world building. It’s a large chunk of the romantic storyline that we are graciously bequeathed with). <br /><br />The point is, I’m sick of the arbitrary use of romance. <b>Stop stuffing it down my throat</b>. If I’m reading a dystopia, I want to read a fucking dystopia. I know y’all will say,<i> “Don’t be a hypocrite. You read Shatter Me and ate that up like you hadn’t seen food in months.”</i> Sure, to an extent, you’re right. <b>BUT</b> (there’s always a but), whilst Shatter Me does the whole romance thing, <b>AT LEAST I WAS GIVEN AN EXCUSE FOR THE DYSTOPIAN WORLD.</b> <br /><br />If you’re a dystopia, it’s not too hard. <b>Just attempt some world building</b>. You can keep your obvious love for romance. JUST DO THE FUCKING WORLDBUILDING. <br /><br />It’s better as a TV show (that’s what nobody wants to hear). Here’s hoping that the sequel does what Throne of Glass did, and comes back brilliantly. <br /><br /><br /><i>Many thanks to the publisher for providing an advanced copy in exchange for an honest review. All quotes used were obtained from uncorrected proof that is subject to change in the final publication.</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13989421693299844528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_617146447" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/617146447" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/617146447?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=series-not-finishing">series-not-finishing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer617146447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2439625312785972987">The 100 has been billed as Battlestar Galactica for teens, and, for once, I totally agree with the marketing. Of course, it's very much season 3 Battlestar where things started going a bit off the rails, with some people on planet in weird costumes and Gaius Baltar becoming some sort of religious figure on the ships. I mean, not exactly, but that's the level of quality the book has. It's not the first season of awesome, and it's not quite the ending where I didn't know what the fuck was happenin</span>
  <span id="freeText2439625312785972987" style="display:none">The 100 has been billed as Battlestar Galactica for teens, and, for once, I totally agree with the marketing. Of course, it's very much season 3 Battlestar where things started going a bit off the rails, with some people on planet in weird costumes and Gaius Baltar becoming some sort of religious figure on the ships. I mean, not exactly, but that's the level of quality the book has. It's not the first season of awesome, and it's not quite the ending where I didn't know what the fuck was happening anymore. What it comes down to is that The 100 is a highly entertaining drama-fest set in space, but not especially deep.<br /><br />Word on the street is that The 100 is set to be a show on the CW. Now, I don't know if it's for certain yet or not, but I can see this making a really great teen show. The reason I'm starting this book review with this particular comment is to help you understand whether you'll enjoy reading the book. If you enjoy CW teen programming with a little bit of a plot and a big heaping helping of teen angst over the top, then The 100 is a good choice for a quick, entertaining read.<br /><br />Morgan uses four third person limited perspectives in The 100: Clarke, Wells, Bellamy, and Glass. Just try and guess their genders based on their names alone! Hint: the first and last are females. Actually, speaking of gender, that's one of the things that I think The 100 did fairly well. Women are not entirely marginalized in this futuristic society, which is a nice change from so much science fiction and dystopian stuff out there. Clarke's actually one of the stronger characters and Glass, though I didn't like her, does make choices for herself.<br /><br />Anyway, these teens live on a spaceship and things are kind of a hot mess on board. There are rules about who can have kids, and capital punishment is really popular with the government. All four of the main characters, except for Bellamy, are Confined, basically imprisoned until their eighteenth birthdays which are rapidly approaching. At that point, they're to have a retrial, but that's just a formality, because no one's being found innocent at retrials anymore. Harsh, man.<br /><br />So the point is that 100 of the teens from Confinement are going to be put on a ship and sent to earth to make sure it's habitable again (more on that later). Then there are some shenanigans and Glass ends up staying on the ship, allowing the reader to find out about all of the drama happening there, and Bellamy gets himself onto the prison ship. The ship goes down to earth and the rebellious teens start in on the romantic drama and trying to set up a rudimentary society, only they're a) rebellious and b) basing their knowledge of how society works off of the ship. All of this means things get pretty serious fast and it's totally a popcorn read.<br /><br />What saves The 100 from being merely a surface read and builds out a bit of depth are the flashbacks in every chapter. These flashbacks show how the teens ended up in Confinement, and slowly reveal how desperate the situation on the ship had gotten. They really raise the stakes and the intensity, as you realize how far each one of these teens is willing to go. <br /><br />As much fun as The 100 is to read, I had some issues with the world building, in that I would like more of it. I mean, the reader does learn that there was some sort of nuclear something or other and Earth is now irradiated. While they're waiting for the radiation to dissipate, they're chilling on this ship. Supposedly the radiation is maybe down to livable levels. What I want to know is roughly how long they've been on the ship and how they got there. Was there a plan in place to escape before things went haywire like in Phoebe North's Starglass? There's really no inkling of that.<br /><br />Also, most of the characters are pretty terrible people, which means that I really don't care if they live or die. Even the nicest of them is such a terrible judge of character that I don't really care what happens to him either. I still had fun reading about them, but there's definitely no emotional investment here.<br /><br />The 100 is the bookish equivalent of a teen TV show, complete with romantic drama, shirtless boys and action scenes. It's fun and a nice choice for when you don't want to have to think too hard, and sometimes that's just the kind of book you need, you know? </span>
  <a data-text-id="2439625312785972987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1597722033?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=multi-povs">multi-povs</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597722033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10955012466329852804">Quick review for a semi-quick read. I had been on the fence about reading Kass Mogan's "The 100" series. I think the tipping point was me finally taking the plunge and watching the CW series of the same name. The first season interested me enough to see what the book series had to offer, only to realize that the book is a horse of a different color entirely (seriously, do not go into the book series thinking that it mirrors the TV series of the same name. Certain characters who die early on in t</span>
  <span id="freeText10955012466329852804" style="display:none">Quick review for a semi-quick read. I had been on the fence about reading Kass Mogan's "The 100" series. I think the tipping point was me finally taking the plunge and watching the CW series of the same name. The first season interested me enough to see what the book series had to offer, only to realize that the book is a horse of a different color entirely (seriously, do not go into the book series thinking that it mirrors the TV series of the same name. Certain characters who die early on in the TV show survive in the book, though some plot parallels and backstories exist). <br /><br />I didn't care much for the novel on the whole, to be honest. Even told through multiple perspectives, I thought that there was a bit too much emphasis on romance alongside the survival aspects and stakes the story put forward. It had a decent framework, but that's all it was - framework. Bare bones, even. I'll admit I was invested enough to see where it wanted to go, but I also felt like banging my head against the wall for numerous reasons. The story is all over the place. Not only is it told between several perspectives (Clarke, Wells, Glass, and Bellamy), but the story jumps willy nilly between past and present events. The characters and presentation feel much more flat than they deserved for the tale. And there were certain lines that were such cheese that I couldn't take them seriously at all. One of the heroes saying that he'd take off his shirt "at some point?" Teens making stupid and morally jarring decisions just to be with the one they love? Pfffffft. Not here for that noise.<br /><br />I'm not saying I didn't care at all about the character tragedies, but it felt jumbled and force-fed, more than I could tolerate for space that could've been used to further develop the world, the rules and regulations in which they are repressed under, and the characters themselves to give them more flesh. I found myself rolling my eyes at the over the top declarations and writing. It just felt...very painful to read at times.<br /><br />I find the TV series problematic in points, but I think the book might be worse for wear. I may decide to pick up the next two books just to see what happens, but I can't say I feel invested in it because the presentation had so much potential only to leave much to be desired. (Literally and figuratively.)<br /><br />Overall score: 1.5/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10955012466329852804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uHoqeZgiOAZG0nQvQvypuoDj0l3vyzS3iKFv5b8rapF3Wv4TppkRW6UzELH679PFlaPZYaUz9YaYcMgTw19ntA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kq1V1yb6pNUf9iXJNRkIJJGctZdJhj+S+wkEia9o/q1djYG9GEGNiPwXQVeNCnJbhNy+qwN+/qPr2KN/0xzziA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Големите успехи на международната сцена се редуват със скандали и неуспешни реформи, но въпреки всичко футболът си извоюва статута на цар на спортовете, който запазва и до ден днешен.\n\nАвторът на книгата Теодор Борисов е доктор по история. От 2008 година е журналист във вестник „Меридиан мач“, на чиито страници публикува множество материали за историята на българския футбол и спорт. Възпитаник на НГДЕК „Константин-Кирил Философ“, през годините той успява по един неподправен начин да съчетае познанията си в сферата на историята и спорта.<\/span>\n  <a <span id="freeTextContainer17334726448287070769">Kass Morgan studied literature at Brown and Oxford, and now resides in Brooklyn, where she lives in constant fear of her Ikea bookcase collapsing and burying her under a mound of science fiction and Victorian novels. </span>
